[4:3:66,152] 3810 - REGIONAL OFFICES AND REGIONAL ADVISORY COMMITTEES  

[4:4:66,169] Twelve Regional Offices and Regional Advisory Committees provide programmatic support to assist with advocacy, capacity  

[4:5:66,179] building, systems change, and implementation of State Plan objectives in Council Regions throughout California. These offices  

[4:6:66,189] and advisory committees provide information and data to the Council to assess regional needs and implementation of the State  

[4:7:66,198] Plan for inclusion in reports to the federal government and the Legislature. These offices also carry out direct service supports  

[4:8:66,208] for pandemic and emergency responses.  

[5:0:66,228] In addition to implementation of State Plan activities, Regional Office staff support the following activities to improve and  

[5:1:66,238] enhance the availability and quality of services for residents of state developmental centers and state-operated community  

[5:2:66,247] facilities:  

[6:0:65,265] • Advocacy services through volunteers recruited by Council staff for individuals who have no legally appointed representative  

[6:1:76,274] to assist them in making choices and decisions.  

[6:2:65,290] • Clients' rights advocacy services to ensure that laws, regulations, and policies pertaining to the rights of persons with  

[6:3:76,300] developmental disabilities are observed.  

[6:4:65,316] • Quality Assessments for individuals who receive community residential services and support.

[5:0:66,226] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,245] 3820 - EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICES AUTHORITY  

[6:1:66,262] Disaster Medical Services Division  

[7:0:66,279] The Disaster Medical Services Division coordinates California's medical response to major disasters by carrying out the  

[7:1:66,289] Authority's mandate to provide medical resources to local governments in support of their disaster response efforts. The  

[7:2:66,299] Division coordinates with the Governor's Office of Emergency Services, the Office of Homeland Security, the California National  

[7:3:66,309] Guard, the California Department of Public Health, and other local, state, and federal agencies, private sector hospitals,  

[7:4:66,318] ambulance companies, and medical supply vendors, to promote and improve disaster preparedness and emergency medical  

[7:5:66,328] response in California.  

[8:0:66,345] Emergency Medical Services Personnel Division  

[9:0:66,363] The Emergency Medical Services Personnel Division is responsible for licensing and enforcement actions of all active  

[9:1:66,373] paramedics throughout the state. The Division develops and implements regulations that set training, certification and licensure  

[9:2:66,382] standards, and the scope of practice for various emergency medical services personnel. The Division also sets standards for,  

[9:3:66,392] and reviews and approves, training programs in public safety first aid, pediatric first aid, CPR,   preventive health practices for  

[9:4:66,402] child day care providers, and school bus drivers. It also develops standards for pre-arrival emergency care instructions and the  

[9:5:66,412] epinephrine auto-injector training program.  

[9:6:66,429] Emergency Medical Services Systems Division  

[10:0:66,446] The Emergency Medical Services Systems Division is responsible for developing and implementing emergency medical  

[10:1:66,456] services systems throughout California, including the support of local Health Information Exchange projects that will allow the  

[10:2:66,466] state to collect more meaningful data so that emergency medical services providers can deliver better patient care. The  

[10:3:66,475] Division also oversees system development and implementation by the local Emergency Medical Services agencies, the  

[10:4:66,485] statewide trauma system, and emergency medical dispatcher and communication standards.   Additionally, it   establishes  

[10:5:66,495] regulations and guidelines for local agencies; reviews and approves local plans to ensure they meet the minimum state  

[10:6:66,505] standards; coordinates injury and illness prevention activities with the California Department of Public Health and the Office of  

[10:7:66,515] Traffic Safety; manages the state's emergency medical services data and quality improvement process; conducts Ambulance  

[10:8:66,524] Exclusive Operating Area evaluations; oversees the operation of California's Poison Control System; and manages the  

[10:9:66,534] Emergency Medical Services for Children programs.

[6:0:66,310] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,329] 3831 - HEALTH CARE QUALITY AND AFFORDABILITY  

[7:0:66,346] The Hospital Fair Billing Program receives and investigates consumer complaints regarding hospital billing and enforces the  

[7:1:66,356] hospital fair pricing policies. The Office of Health Care Affordability (OHCA) has three primary responsibilities: managing cost  

[7:2:66,366] growth targets, monitoring system performance, and assessing market consolidation. OHCA will collect, analyze, and publicly  

[7:3:66,375] report data on total health care expenditures, and enforce cost growth targets set by a new Health Care Affordability Board. To  

[7:4:66,385] ensure a balanced approach to managing costs, OHCA will monitor system performance by measuring quality, equity, adoption  

[7:5:66,395] of alternative payment models, investment in primary care and behavioral health, and workforce stability. Through cost and  

[7:6:66,405] market impact reviews, OHCA will analyze transactions that are likely to significantly impact on market competition, the state’s  

[7:7:66,415] ability to meet cost targets, or affordability for consumers and purchasers. Based on results of the review, OHCA will then  

[7:8:66,424] coordinate with other state agencies to address consolidation as appropriate.  

[7:9:66,442] 3835 - HEALTH CARE WORKFORCE  

[8:0:66,461] The Health Care Workforce Program improves access to medical, mental, and dental health care providers in underserved  

[8:1:66,471] areas throughout California. The Program conducts research to identify areas of unmet need and administers grants that  

[8:2:66,481] provide financial incentives to individuals and institutions to increase the number of providers in those areas. The Program  

[8:3:66,490] promotes health care workforce diversity and cultural competency. It includes the following programs:  

[8:4:65,508] • Song-Brown Health Care Workforce Training Program  

[8:5:65,523] • Mental Health Services Act Workforce Education and Training Program  

[8:6:65,539] • Health Professions Careers Opportunity Program  

[8:7:65,555] • Health Workforce Pilot Projects Program  

[8:8:65,571] • Health Workforce Research Data Center  

[8:9:65,587] • California's Primary Care Office, which includes:  

[8:10:74,604] ◦ Shortage Designation Program  

[8:11:74,620] ◦ State Office of Rural Health 

[8:12:74,635] ◦ J-1 Visa Waiver Program  

[9:0:65,659] • California Health Workforce Education and Training Council  

[9:1:65,674] • Scholarship Programs  

[10:0:65,690] • Loan Repayment Programs, including the California State Loan Repayment Program, Steven M. Thompson Physician Corps  

[10:1:76,700] Loan Repayment Program and Licensed Mental Health Services Provider Education Program  

[10:2:65,716] • Children and Youth Behavioral Health Initiative Workforce Programs

[3:0:66,68] 3840 - FACILITIES DEVELOPMENT  

[4:0:66,86] The Facilities Development Program safeguards public health, safety, and general welfare through regulation of the design and  

[4:1:66,96] construction of health care facilities, including compliance with seismic safety requirements, to ensure they are capable of  

[4:2:66,105] providing sustained services to the public.  

[4:3:66,123] 3845 - CAL-MORTGAGE LOAN INSURANCE  

[5:0:66,142] The Cal-Mortgage Program is modeled after federal home mortgage insurance programs and insures loans to public and  

[5:1:66,152] nonprofit health care facilities for construction, renovation, and expansion projects. The Program underwrites loans, monitors  

[5:2:66,162] the Cal-Mortgage insured loan portfolio, and administers the Health Facility Construction Loan Insurance Fund. By facilitating  

[5:3:66,171] access to private capital at no cost to taxpayers, the Program has improved the delivery of health care throughout California.  

[5:4:66,189] The Distressed Hospital Loan Program requires HCAI and the California Health Facilities Financing Authority (CHFFA) to  

[5:5:66,198] collaboratively administer the Distressed Hospital Loan Program to offer interest-free, working capital loans to non-profit and  

[5:6:66,208] publicly-operated financially distressed hospitals, including hospitals that belong to integrated health care systems with no more  

[5:7:66,218] than two separately licensed hospitals in California that are facing a risk of closure, while they implement turnaround strategies  

[5:8:66,228] to regain financial viability.   HCAI contracts with CHFFA through an Inter-Agency Agreement to administer the loan program. 

[5:9:66,238] The founding legislation also includes provisions requiring hospitals to submit quarterly financial data to HCAI, for use in  

[5:10:66,247] monitoring the financial health of hospitals throughout the state.  

[5:11:66,265] 3855 - HEALTH CARE INFORMATION AND QUALITY ANALYSIS 

[6:0:66,282] The Health Care Information Program sets standards for, collects, and maintains financial and utilization data from  

[7:0:66,292] approximately 9,500 licensed health facilities in California, as well as comprehensive demographic, diagnostic, and treatment  

[7:1:66,301] data for all patients discharged from licensed hospitals, treated in emergency departments, or having had an ambulatory  

[7:2:66,311] surgery procedure in hospital surgical clinics. This information is used by health care policymakers, health care providers,  

[7:3:66,321] health planners, public and private sector health care purchasers, researchers, consumers, and the media. To further this  

[7:4:66,331] mission, the Health Care Information Program is implementing new health care cost transparency data programs to collect and  

[7:5:66,341] analyze prescription drug cost data, hospital supplier diversity data, hospital quality and equity data, and health care payment  

[7:6:66,350] data to improve transparency, inform policy decisions, reduce disparities, and reduce health care costs.

[8:1:66,397] and administrative services to HCAI.

[8:0:184,500] 4150   Department of Managed Health Care  

[9:0:66,521] The Department of Managed Health Care protects health care consumers   and ensures a stable health care delivery system in  

[9:1:66,531] California. The Department achieves this mission by:  

[9:2:65,548] • Licensing and regulating the full scope of managed care models, including all Health Maintenance Organizations (HMO),  

[9:3:76,558] Preferred Provider Organizations (PPO), Exclusive Provider Organizations (EPO), Point-of-Service (POS) products and  

[9:4:76,568] Medi-Cal managed care plans. The Department also licenses and conducts financial reviews of Medicare Advantage and  

[9:5:76,577] Part D plans and licenses and regulates specialized health plans including chiropractic, dental, vision, psychological  

[9:6:76,587] (behavioral health) and pharmacy.  

[9:7:65,603] • Enforcing the Knox-Keene Health Care Service Plan Act of 1975, as amended.  

[9:8:65,619] • Conducting medical surveys and financial examinations to verify that health plans are complying with the law and are  

[9:9:76,628] financially stable to serve their enrollees.  

[9:10:65,644] • Operating a 24-hour-a-day Help Center to resolve health care consumer complaints and administer the Independent Medical  

[9:11:76,654] Review program.

[5:0:66,177] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,195] 3870 - HEALTH PLAN PROGRAM  

[6:0:66,215] The Health Plan Program's primary objective is to regulate managed health care plans and assist consumers to resolve  

[6:1:66,225] disputes with health plans. The program's key functions to achieve this objective are to: license managed health care plans,  

[6:2:66,234] conduct routine and non-routine financial exams and medical surveys, review proposed premium rate increases, assist  

[6:3:66,244] consumers with health care issues and enable managed health care patients to receive the medical care and services to which  

[6:4:66,254] they are entitled, and operate a consumer services toll-free complaint line (1-888-466-2219).

[14:1:66,653] programs, planning, policies, and partnerships that increase choices, equity, and well-being for all Californians as we age.  

[14:2:66,671] As the federally designated State Unit on Aging, the Department administers federal Older Americans Act programs that  

[14:3:66,680] provide a wide variety of community-based supportive services, administers the Health Insurance Counseling and Advocacy  

[14:4:66,690] Program that provides individualized counseling to Medicare beneficiaries, and administers and oversees the development and  

[14:5:66,700] expansion of the Aging and Disability Resource Connection program to provide person centered care to older adults and adults  

[14:6:66,710] living with disabilities. The Department also administers two Medi-Cal programs; it contracts directly with agencies that operate

[7:0:66,471] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[7:1:66,490] 3890 - NUTRITION  

[8:0:66,507] The Nutrition Program provides nutritionally balanced meals, nutrition education, and nutrition counseling to individuals 60  

[8:1:66,517] years of age or older. In addition to promoting better health through improved nutrition, the program focuses on reducing the  

[8:2:66,527] isolation of the elderly and providing a link to other social and supportive services such as transportation, information and  

[8:3:66,537] assistance, employment, and education.  

[8:4:66,554] 3895 - SENIOR COMMUNITY EMPLOYMENT SERVICE  

[9:0:66,574] The federal Senior Community Service Employment Program, Title V of the Older Americans Act, provides part-time subsidized  

[9:1:66,583] training and employment in community service agencies for low-income persons 55 years of age and older. The program also  

[9:2:66,593] promotes transition to unsubsidized employment.  

[9:3:66,610] 3900 - SUPPORTIVE SERVICES  

[10:0:66,628] This program provides supportive services in the community to adults 60 years of age or older, their family caregivers,  

[10:1:66,637] grandparents caring for grandchildren, and residents of long-term care facilities. Services include information and assistance,  

[10:2:66,647] legal assistance, transportation, respite in-home support, senior center activities, elder abuse prevention, and the Long-Term  

[10:3:66,657] Care Ombudsman. Older Americans Act Titles III and VII fund these services to enable individuals to access the support  

[10:4:66,667] necessary for them to remain independent in their communities, continue in their caregiving role, and/or receive long-term care  

[10:5:66,677] services appropriate to their needs.  

[11:0:66,694] 3905 - COMMUNITY-BASED PROGRAMS AND PROJECTS  

[12:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:0:163,32] 4170   California Department of Aging - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] This program includes the community-based Health Insurance Counseling and Advocacy Program (HICAP). HICAP provides  

[3:1:66,78] personalized counseling, community education, and outreach events for Medicare beneficiaries. HICAP is the primary local  

[3:2:66,88] source for accurate and objective information and assistance with Medicare benefits, prescription drug plans, and health plans.  

[3:3:66,105] 3910 - MEDI-CAL PROGRAMS  

[4:0:66,123] This program includes oversight of the Multipurpose Senior Services Program (MSSP) and Community-Based Adult Services  

[4:1:66,132] (CBAS) program. Under a 1915(c) Medicaid home and community-based services waiver, MSSP provides health and social  

[4:2:66,142] care management to prevent premature and unnecessary long-term care institutionalization of frail adults aged 65 or older who  

[4:3:66,152] otherwise would be placed in a nursing facility. CBAS is a community-based day health program that provides services to  

[4:4:66,162] adults 18 years of age or over who are at risk of needing institutional care due to chronic medical, cognitive, or mental health  

[4:5:66,171] conditions and/or disabilities. The Department certifies CBAS centers for participation in the Medi-Cal Program.  

[4:6:66,189] 3915 - POLICY AND PLANNING  

[5:0:66,206] This program is responsible for Aging policy research, analysis, and development for the State’s Aging programs. The program  

[5:1:66,216] specifically addresses policy and planning related to inclusion and isolation prevention, equity-in-aging, housing and livable  

[5:2:66,226] communities, and health in the home and community.

[8:0:66,328] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[8:1:66,347] 3930 - COMMISSION ON AGING  

[9:0:66,364] The Commission works with the Legislature, government officials and public, nonprofit and private-sector organizations to  

[9:1:66,374] address public policy and issues that impact older Californians. The Commission prepares, publishes and disseminates  

[9:2:66,384] information, findings and recommendations regarding the well-being of older adults, advises the California Department of Aging  

[9:3:66,394] on the development of the State Plan on Aging and monitors Plan implementation. As part of its information-gathering  

[9:4:66,404] responsibility, the Commission holds meetings and public hearings around the State. The Commission held membership on the  

[9:5:66,413] Governor’s Master Plan for Aging Stakeholder Advisory Committee and currently holds membership on the Elder and Disability  

[9:6:66,423] Justice Coordinating Council, Disability and Aging Community Living Advisory Committee, Equity in Aging Advisory Committee,  

[9:7:66,433] Data Exchange Framework Stakeholder Advisory Committee and Aging and Disability Resource Connection Advisory  

[9:8:66,443] Committee. The Commission also provides administrative support for the Area Agency on Aging Advisory Councils of  

[9:9:66,452] California, which is supported solely by voluntary contributions made through a check-off box included on the State income tax  

[9:10:66,462] form.

[4:0:169,130] 4260   State Department of Health Care Services  

[5:0:66,151] The mission of the State Department of Health Care Services (DHCS) is to provide Californians with access to affordable,  

[6:0:66,160] integrated, high-quality health care, including medical, dental, mental health, substance use treatment services, and long-term  

[6:1:66,170] care. To fulfill its mission, DHCS finances and administers a number of individual health care service delivery programs,  

[7:0:66,180] including the state's Medicaid Program (Medi-Cal), which provides health care services to low-income persons and families  

[7:1:66,190] who meet defined eligibility requirements.

[5:0:66,222] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,241] 3960010 - MEDICAL CARE SERVICES (MEDI-CAL)  

[6:0:66,258] Medi-Cal is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care services to low-income Californians. Medi-Cal  

[6:1:66,268] provides access to high-quality health care services in a fiscally prudent manner through both fee-for-service and managed  

[6:2:66,278] care delivery systems. Medi-Cal activities are carried out through the following functional groups: Health Care Benefits and  

[6:3:66,288] Eligibility; Health Care Delivery Systems; Health Care Financing; Behavioral Health; Audits and Investigations; Enterprise Data  

[6:4:66,298] and Information Management; and Program Operations.  

[6:5:66,315] 3960023 - CHILDREN'S MEDICAL SERVICES  

[7:0:66,332] Children's Medical Services is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care services to low-income and  

[7:1:66,342] seriously ill children, including the Child Health and Disability Prevention Program, the Genetically Handicapped Persons  

[7:2:66,352] Program, and the California Children's Services Program. These services are provided through Health Care Delivery Systems’  

[7:3:66,361] Integrated Systems of Care Division.  

[7:4:66,379] 3960032 - PRIMARY, RURAL, AND INDIAN HEALTH  

[8:0:66,396] Primary, Rural, and Indian Health is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care to Californians in rural  

[8:1:66,406] areas and to underserved populations through the following programs: Indian Health Program, American Indian Maternal  

[8:2:66,416] Support Services, and Tribal Emergency Preparedness Program.  

[8:3:66,433] 3960050 - OTHER CARE SERVICES  

[9:0:66,450] The Department is also responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of non-Medi-Cal community health services;  

[9:1:66,460] mental health and substance use disorder services; cancer screening services to low-income, under-insured, or uninsured  

[9:2:66,470] individuals; and prostate cancer treatment services to low-income, under-insured, or uninsured men. These services are  

[9:3:66,479] provided through the   Behavioral Health Community   Services Division, Behavioral Health Licensing and Certification Division,  

[9:4:66,489] the Every Woman Counts Program, and the Prostate Cancer Treatment Program.

[6:0:207,254] 4265   Department of Public Health  

[7:0:66,275] The California Department of Public Health (DPH) is dedicated to optimizing the health and well-being of all Californians  

[7:1:66,285] through the following core activities:  

[7:2:65,302] • Protecting the public from communicable diseases.  

[8:0:65,318] • Protecting the public from unhealthy and unsafe environments, and improving social determinants of health and healthy  

[8:1:76,328] communities.  

[9:0:65,343] • Preventing disease, injury, disability, and premature death; and reducing or eliminating health disparities by embedding  

[9:1:76,353] health and mental health equity language, tools, and approaches into all public health and partner agency policies, practices,  

[9:2:76,363] programs, systems, and resource allocation.  

[9:3:65,379] • Preparing for and responding to public health emergencies.  

[10:0:65,395] • Producing and disseminating data to evaluate population health status; inform people, institutions and communities; and to  

[10:1:76,404] guide public health strategies, programs, and actions.  

[11:0:65,420] • Promoting healthy lifestyles for individuals and families in their communities and workplaces.  

[11:1:65,436] • Providing access to quality, population-based health services.  

[12:0:66,453] Because DPH's programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program to support  

[12:1:66,463] this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[4:0:66,378] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:0:66,397] 4040010 - Emergency Preparedness and Response  

[6:0:66,414] The Emergency Preparedness and Response program provides expertise, leadership, and dedicated support for the  

[6:1:66,424] coordination of emergency planning, preparedness, response, and recovery efforts for all public health emergencies and  

[6:2:66,434] disasters, including natural disasters, acts of terrorism, and infectious diseases. The program oversees statewide public health  

[6:3:66,444] disaster planning; supports medical care and public health systems to plan for and respond to medical surge; coordinates and  

[6:4:66,453] facilitates efforts between federal, state, and local entities; and maintains other risk communications and response systems  

[6:5:66,463] during emergencies and disasters. The program also administers federal and state funds to support public health emergency  

[6:6:66,473] preparedness and response activities at the state and local levels.  

[6:7:66,490] 4045 - PUBLIC AND ENVIRONMENTAL HEALTH  

[7:0:66,507] The Public and Environmental Health programs provide public health services of: communicable disease control; chronic  

[7:1:66,517] disease and injury prevention; environmental public health; maternal, child, and family health; and vital records. These  

[7:2:66,527] programs function as part of the greater public health system throughout California.  

[7:3:66,544] 4045010 - Healthy Communities  

[8:0:66,561] The Healthy Communities program works to prevent and control chronic diseases such as cancer, cardiovascular diseases,  

[8:1:66,571] asthma, Alzheimer's, and diabetes; to reduce the prevalence of obesity; to reduce tobacco use; to improve oral health through  

[8:2:66,581] prevention, education, and community efforts; to provide training programs for the public health workforce; to prevent and  

[8:3:66,591] control injuries, violence, deaths, and diseases related to behavioral, environmental, and occupational factors; to promote and  

[8:4:66,601] support safe, equitable, and healthy environments in communities and workplaces; to prevent substance and gambling  

[8:5:66,610] addiction and treat gambling disorder; and to support suicide prevention efforts. This program includes the California Tobacco  

[8:6:66,620] Control Program, Childhood Lead Poisoning Prevention Branch, Chronic Disease Control Branch, Chronic Disease  

[8:7:66,630] Surveillance and Research Branch, Environmental Health Investigations Branch, Nutrition Education and Obesity Prevention  

[8:8:66,640] Branch, Occupational Health Branch, Injury and Violence Prevention Branch, Substance and Addiction Prevention Branch, and  

[8:9:66,649] the Office of Oral Health.  

[8:10:66,667] 4045023 - Infectious Diseases  

[9:0:66,684] The Infectious Diseases program works to prevent and control infectious diseases such as: HIV/AIDS, viral hepatitis, influenza  

[9:1:66,694] and other vaccine-preventable illnesses, sexually transmitted diseases, tuberculosis, emerging infections, and foodborne  

[9:2:66,704] illnesses. This program includes the Division of Communicable Disease Control, the Office of AIDS, the Office of Binational  

[9:3:66,713] Border Health, and the Office of Refugee Health.  

[10:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:412,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — HHS   93 

[2:0:172,32] 4265   Department of Public Health - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] 4045032 - Family Health  

[4:0:66,86] The Family Health program works to improve the health and well-being of individuals, pregnant people, children and youth as  

[4:1:66,96] well as reduce disparities in perinatal health outcomes. This program includes the Genetic Disease Screening Program;  

[4:2:66,105] Maternal, Child, and Adolescent Health; and the Special Supplemental Nutrition Program for Women, Infants, and Children.  

[4:3:66,123] 4045041 - Health Statistics and Informatics  

[5:0:66,140] The Health Statistics and Informatics program works to improve the public’s health by managing information systems and  

[5:1:66,150] facilitating the collection, validation, analysis, and dissemination of health statistics and demographic information on the  

[5:2:66,159] California population. This program includes Vital Records and Public Health Informatics.  

[5:3:66,177] 4045050 - County Health Services  

[6:0:66,194] The County Health Services program supports county-based public health information and services, including the Medical  

[6:1:66,204] Marijuana Identification Card Program.  

[6:2:66,221] 4045059 - Environmental Health  

[7:0:66,238] The Environmental Health program works to protect and improve the health of all California residents by utilizing inspection,  

[7:1:66,248] technical assistance, regulatory, investigation, and emergency response activities to improve the safety of foods, industrial  

[7:2:66,258] hemp products, drugs, and medical devices; conduct underage tobacco enforcement; oversee the use of radiation and  

[7:3:66,268] radioactive materials; regulate medical waste; and conduct other environmental management programs. The program includes  

[7:4:66,277] the Division of Food and Drug Safety and the Division of Radiation Safety and Environmental Management.  

[7:5:66,295] 4045068 - Laboratory Sciences  

[8:0:66,312] The Center for Laboratory Sciences   provides laboratory testing services, technical consultation, and leadership for the state  

[8:1:66,322] Public Health Laboratory system to protect Californians from the threat of infectious and environmental diseases. The   Center  

[8:2:66,331] includes the Drinking Water and   Radiation Laboratory, Environmental Health Laboratory, Food and   Drug Laboratory, Infant  

[8:3:66,341] Botulism Treatment and   Prevention Program, Microbial Diseases Laboratory, and Viral and   Rickettsial   Disease Laboratory. The  

[8:4:66,351] Center   provides laboratory testing services to support public health surveillance programs; research for disease diagnosis,  

[8:5:66,361] characterization, investigation, and control; and subject matter expertise to inform effective decision-making.  

[8:6:66,378] 4050 - LICENSING AND CERTIFICATION  

[8:7:66,395] 4050010 - Health Facilities  

[9:0:66,413] The Health Facilities program regulates the quality of care in over 14,000 public and private health facilities, clinics, and  

[9:1:66,422] agencies throughout the state; licenses nursing home administrators; certifies nurse assistants, home health aides, and  

[9:2:66,432] hemodialysis technicians; and oversees the prevention, surveillance and reporting of healthcare-associated infections in  

[9:3:66,442] California's health facilities.  

[9:4:66,459] 4050019 - Laboratory Field Services  

[10:0:66,476] The Laboratory Field Services   program regulates California clinical and public health laboratory, blood bank, biologics, and  

[10:1:66,486] tissue bank quality standards through licensure and oversight of approximately 27,000   clinical laboratories, public health  

[10:2:66,496] laboratories, blood banks, biologics facilities, and tissue banks operating in California; and approximately 65,000   California  

[10:3:66,506] laboratory personnel in more than 30 different categories of laboratory personnel including phlebotomists, cytotechnologists,  

[10:4:66,516] medical laboratory technicians, clinical laboratory scientists, public health microbiologists, and clinical reproductive biologists.

[12:0:176,512] 4300   Department of Developmental Services  

[13:0:66,533] The Department of Developmental Services is responsible under the Lanterman Developmental Disabilities Services Act for  

[13:1:66,542] overseeing the coordination and delivery of services and supports that persons with developmental disabilities need to lead  

[13:2:66,552] more independent and productive lives and to make choices and decisions about their lives. The Department sets broad policy  

[13:3:66,562] and provides leadership for developmental services statewide; establishes priorities and standards within which the  

[13:4:66,572] developmental services program operates; monitors, reviews, and evaluates service delivery; and helps to remediate problems  

[13:5:66,582] that arise. Services are delivered through a statewide network of 21 private, nonprofit, locally based community agencies  

[13:6:66,591] known as regional centers as well as through state-operated facilities. The Department, through contracts with the 21 regional  

[13:7:66,601] centers, oversees through audits and other review the coordination of services to persons with developmental disabilities;  

[13:8:66,611] provides that such services are planned, provided, and meet the needs and choices of these individuals at each stage of their  

[13:9:66,621] lives; and, to the extent possible, accomplishes these goals in the individual's home community.  

[14:0:66,638] Because the Department of Developmental Services' programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has  

[14:1:66,648] a capital outlay program to support this need. For specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure  

[14:2:66,657] Overview."

[7:0:66,428] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[8:0:66,447] 4140 - COMMUNITY SERVICES PROGRAM  

[9:0:66,466] Through the network of regional centers, the Department contracts with regional centers to support the development and  

[9:1:66,476] maintenance of services for eligible persons with developmental disabilities who reside in the community. The regional centers  

[9:2:66,486] directly provide or coordinate the following services and supports: (1) information and referral, (2) assessment and diagnosis,  

[9:3:66,496] (3) counseling, (4) lifelong individualized planning and service coordination, (5) purchase of necessary services included in the  

[9:4:66,505] individual program plan, (6) assistance in finding and using community and other resources, (7) advocacy for the protection of  

[9:5:66,515] legal, civil, and service rights, (8) early intervention services for infants and their families, (9) family support, (10) planning,  

[9:6:66,525] placement, and monitoring for 24-hour out-of-home care, (11) training and educational opportunities for individuals and families,  

[9:7:66,535] (12) community education about developmental disabilities, and (13) habilitation services.  

[10:0:66,552] 4145 - STATE-OPERATED RESIDENTIAL AND COMMUNITY FACILITIES PROGRAM  

[11:0:66,569] The Department currently operates two residential facilities: Fairview Developmental Center (Orange County) and Porterville  

[11:1:66,579] Developmental Center (Tulare County). Secure treatment services are provided at the Porterville Developmental Center  

[11:2:66,589] for   individuals who have been found incompetent to stand trial due to their developmental disability or are dangerous to  

[11:3:66,599] themselves or others and civilly committed to the facility by court order. The Department is projected to operate seven  

[11:4:66,608] Stabilization, Training, Assistance, and Reintegration (STAR) residences in Northern, Central, and Southern California   to  

[11:5:66,618] provide acute crisis services in the community. The Department also leases one small community facility for persons who  

[11:6:66,628] require specialized behavioral interventions: Canyon Springs, a 63-bed facility in Cathedral City (Riverside County).  

[12:0:66,645] All   residential facilities are licensed as General Acute Care Hospitals with distinct parts for skilled nursing care and intermediate  

[12:1:66,655] care. Canyon Springs operates as an intermediate care facility and STAR residences operate as community crisis homes.  

[12:2:66,665] Services at all facilities involve the provision of active treatment through residential and day programs on a 24-hour basis,  

[12:3:66,674] including appropriate medical and dental care, health maintenance activities, and assistance with activities of daily living,  

[12:4:66,684] training, education, and employment.  

[13:0:66,701] Individuals served in the STAR crisis   residences are committed by a court order to the Department for suitable treatment and  

[13:1:66,711] habilitation services during a crisis and are provided services and supports necessary to prepare them for return to their home  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,68] or to transition to a new living option. The primary objective of this program   is to provide a safety net of services that include  

[3:1:66,78] providing care, treatment, crisis services, and habilitation services to residents based upon assessed need and as outlined in  

[3:2:66,88] each person's Individual Program Plan. These services are offered in the most efficient, effective, and least restrictive manner  

[3:3:66,98] to all individuals referred by the regional centers and/or the judicial system and are designed to teach individuals the skills for  

[3:4:66,108] increased independence, provide for preservation or improvement of health and welfare, and enhance personal competence in  

[3:5:66,117] all areas of daily living.  

[4:0:66,135] 4149 - PROGRAM ADMINISTRATION  

[5:0:66,154] The objective of this program is to: (1) provide overall management, planning and policy development, legal, legislative, audit,  

[5:1:66,164] and administrative services; (2) manage revenue and reimbursement collections from federal and state programs, insurance  

[5:2:66,174] companies, and private payers for the cost of services; (3) monitor regional center operations for compliance with statute,  

[5:3:66,183] regulations, and their contract with the Department; (4) provide central administrative and clinical management services to  

[5:4:66,193] the   state-operated residential and community   facilities to oversee the quality of services provided, compliance with state  

[5:5:66,203] licensing and federal certification requirements, protection of consumers and staff, and maintenance of facility structures and  

[5:6:66,213] grounds; and (5) oversee areas that include the development of policies and procedures for developmental center operations,  

[5:7:66,223] law enforcement and protective services, facility population management, program and fiscal oversight, and facility planning  

[5:8:66,232] and support.

[10:0:66,504] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[11:0:66,523] The Department of Developmental Services is responsible for the operation and maintenance of facilities under its control,  

[11:1:66,532] including two state-owned and operated 24-hour care facilities and related buildings, grounds, and infrastructure. The facilities  

[11:2:66,542] are Fairview Developmental Center in Orange County and Porterville Developmental Center in Tulare County.  

[11:3:66,559] The developmental centers are comprised of approximately 2.3 million gross square feet in 319 buildings on 784 acres. As of  

[11:4:66,569] February 2020, the Fairview Developmental Center and the Porterville General Treatment Area transitioned all former residents  

[11:5:66,579] to community living. The Department will continue to maintain the Fairview property in warm shutdown mode until disposition of  

[11:6:66,589] the property. The Department is projected to operate seven Stabilization, Training, Assistance, and Reintegration (STAR)  

[11:7:66,598] residences that provide acute crisis services in the community. Additionally, the Department is responsible for the maintenance  

[11:8:66,608] of interior finishes and equipment at Canyon Springs, a 57,000-square-foot leased facility in Riverside County. These facilities  

[11:9:66,618] support the Department's mission in providing medical, dental, and nursing care; active treatment; supervision; education; and  

[11:10:66,628] vocational training for residents with developmental disabilities committed to a state-operated facility.

[10:0:201,456] 4440   Department of State Hospitals  

[11:0:66,477] The Department of State Hospitals manages the nation's largest inpatient forensic mental health hospital system. Its mission is  

[11:1:66,487] to provide evaluation and treatment in a safe and responsible manner, by leading innovation and excellence across a  

[11:2:66,497] continuum of care and settings. The Department is responsible for the daily care and provision of mental health treatment of its  

[11:3:66,506] patients. The Department oversees five state hospitals located in Atascadero, Coalinga, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, and  

[11:4:66,516] Patton,   and employs over 13,000 staff. In addition to the state hospital treatment,   the Department provides services in  

[11:5:66,526] contracted jail-based competency treatment (JBCT), community-based restoration (CBR), community inpatient facilities and  

[11:6:66,536] pre-trial felony mental health diversion programs, and the conditional release program (CONREP).  

[11:7:66,553] Because the Department programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program to  

[11:8:66,563] support this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[8:0:66,536] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[8:1:66,555] 4400 - ADMINISTRATION  

[9:0:66,572] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health  

[9:1:66,582] services to patients admitted into Department of State Hospitals facilities. Program Administration includes headquarters  

[9:2:66,592] functions such as: policy development and management, program oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight,  

[9:3:66,601] data research, fiscal, personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services.  

[9:4:66,619] Hospital Administration includes centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care but are administered  

[9:5:66,628] centrally from headquarters.  

[9:6:66,646] 4400010 - HEADQUARTERS ADMINISTRATION  

[10:0:66,663] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health  

[10:1:66,673] services to patients admitted into   system of care. Headquarters Administration includes headquarters functions such as: policy  

[10:2:66,683] development and management, healthcare standards compliance, statewide patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight,  

[10:3:66,692] data research, fiscal, personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services.

[0:0:66,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — HHS   146 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:166,32] 4440   Department of State Hospitals - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters includes a Hospital Administration component. Hospital Administration includes  

[3:1:66,78] centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care in DSH hospitals but are administered centrally from  

[3:2:66,88] headquarters such as: technology services, hospital police and fire oversight, patient referral management, clinical recruitment,  

[3:3:66,98] patient benefit and billing management, and Medicare revenue collection.  

[4:0:66,115] 4410 - STATE HOSPITALS  

[5:0:66,132] The state hospital system includes five state hospitals located at Atascadero, Coalinga, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, and  

[5:1:66,142] Patton. Mental health treatment services at all facilities are delivered by clinical teams who provide full-time inpatient care to  

[5:2:66,152] those with serious mental illness and are   predominantly ordered for treatment by a criminal or civil court or by the Board of  

[5:3:66,162] Parole Hearings. To a lesser extent, the Department of State Hospitals also receives referrals for state hospital treatment from  

[5:4:66,171] county behavioral health departments or the public guardians, as well as from the California Department of Corrections and  

[5:5:66,181] Rehabilitation (CDCR). The state hospitals treat the following types of patients: civil commitments under the Lanterman-Petris-

[5:6:66,191] Short Act (LPS); forensic commitments such as Incompetent to Stand Trial (IST), Not Guilty by Reason of Insanity (NGI),  

[5:7:66,201] Sexually Violent Predators (SVP), and Offender with a Mental Health Disorder (OMD); and prisoners with mental illness  

[5:8:66,211] ( Coleman ) from CDCR.  

[6:0:66,228] 4410010 - ATASCADERO  

[7:0:66,245] The Department of State Hospitals-Atascadero opened in 1954 and is located on the Central Coast of California in Atascadero  

[7:1:66,255] (San Luis Obispo County). The hospital is a self-contained psychiatric hospital constructed within a security perimeter. The  

[7:2:66,265] majority of the all-male patient population is remanded for treatment by   Superior Courts or by CDCR pursuant to various  

[7:3:66,274] sections of the California Penal Code   and the Welfare and Institutions Code.  

[8:0:66,292] DSH-Atascadero primarily serves the following four patient types: OMD,  Coleman   patients from CDCR, IST, and   NGI.  

[9:0:66,309] 4410020 - COALINGA  

[10:0:66,326] The Department of State Hospitals-Coalinga opened in 2005 and is located on the western edge of Fresno County. The  

[10:1:66,336] hospital is California’s newest forensic mental health hospital and was created to primarily treat SVPs. It is a self-contained  

[10:2:66,346] psychiatric hospital constructed with a security perimeter. CDCR provides perimeter security as well as transportation of  

[10:3:66,356] patients to outside medical services and court proceedings. The majority of the all-male patient population is remanded for  

[10:4:66,365] treatment by   Superior Courts or CDCR pursuant to various sections of the California Penal Code and the Welfare and  

[10:5:66,375] Institutions Code.  

[11:0:66,392] DSH-Coalinga primarily serves SVP, OMD and  Coleman   patients from CDCR.  

[12:0:66,410] 4410030 - METROPOLITAN  

[13:0:66,427] The Department of State Hospitals-Metropolitan opened in 1916 and is located in Norwalk (Los Angeles County). The hospital  

[13:1:66,437] is an open style campus with a security perimeter. Due to concerns raised by the community, DSH-Metropolitan maintains a  

[13:2:66,446] formal agreement with the City of Norwalk and the Los Angeles County Sheriff not to accept patients charged with murder or a  

[13:3:66,456] sex crime, or that are at high risk for escape.  

[14:0:66,474] DSH-Metropolitan primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, OMD, and NGI.  

[15:0:66,491] 4410040 - NAPA  

[16:0:66,508] The Department of State Hospitals-Napa opened in 1875 and is located in Napa County. The hospital   was the first of the  

[16:1:66,518] five   State Hospitals and is   the oldest California state hospital still in operation.   It has an open style campus with a security  

[16:2:66,528] perimeter.  

[17:0:66,545] DSH-Napa primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, OMD, and NGI.  

[18:0:66,562] 4410050 - PATTON  

[19:0:66,579] The Department of State Hospitals-Patton opened in 1893 and is located in San Bernardino County. The hospital has an open  

[19:1:66,589] style campus with a security perimeter. CDCR correctional officers provide perimeter security and transportation at DSH-Patton  

[19:2:66,599] as well as transportation of patients to outside medical services and some court proceedings.  

[20:0:66,616] DSH-Patton primarily serves the following five patient types: LPS, IST, OMD, NGI and female  Coleman   patients from CDCR.  

[21:0:66,634] 4410060 - HOSPITAL POLICE OFFICER ACADEMY  

[22:0:66,651] The Department of State Hospitals Police Officer Academy is overseen by the Office of Protective Services, which is a full  

[22:1:66,661] service law enforcement agency that protects the safety and security of the state hospital facilities, staff and patients. The  

[22:2:66,670] Department provides training standards, model programs, cultural competency, program development, and a comprehensive  

[22:3:66,680] training plan to all protective services staff. 

[23:0:66,697] 4420 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:407,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — HHS   147 

[2:0:166,32] 4440   Department of State Hospitals - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] The Conditional Release Program is the statewide system of community-based services for specified forensic patients.  

[3:1:66,78] Mandated as a state responsibility by the Governor's Mental Health Initiative of 1984, the program began operations on  

[3:2:66,88] January 1, 1986.  

[4:0:66,105] 4420010 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM  

[5:0:66,123] The Conditional Release Program General/Non-Sexually Violent Predators is comprised of   NGI, OMD, and IST. Individuals  

[5:1:66,132] suitable for this program may be recommended by the state hospital medical director to the courts for outpatient treatment.  

[5:2:66,142] Currently, DSH contracts with seven county-operated and three private organizations   serving all 58 counties in the state with  

[5:3:66,152] non-SVP commitments.  

[6:0:66,169] 4420020 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM -   SEXUALLY VIOLENT PREDATORS  

[7:0:66,186] The Conditional Release Program-Sexually Violent Predators was added to the Conditional Release Program effective January  

[7:1:66,196] 1, 1996 per Welfare and Institutions Code 6604. Prior to the conditional release of the first   SVP in 2003,   conditional release  

[7:2:66,206] providers did not have treatment services that would allow them to accept sexually violent predators as patients, requiring the  

[7:3:66,216] Department of State Hospitals to enter into an annual contract with a single private provider serving 58 counties. Current  

[7:4:66,226] statute requires SVPs be conditionally released to their county of domicile and sufficient funding be available to provide  

[7:5:66,235] treatment and supervision services when an   SVP is conditionally released into the community by court order.  

[8:0:66,253] 4430 - CONTRACTED PATIENT SERVICES  

[9:0:66,270] The Department of State Hospitals contracts with local entities to provide mental health services to some of its patients outside  

[9:1:66,280] of state hospital facilities. This includes the   Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Centers, Jail-Based Competency  

[9:2:66,289] Treatment programs, IST Diversion programs, Community-Based Restoration programs and Community Inpatient Facility  

[9:3:66,299] programs.  

[10:0:66,316] 4430010 - ADMISSION, EVALUATION, STABILIZATION CENTER 

[11:0:66,334] The Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center in the Kern County Jail receives   IST patients committed to the  

[11:1:66,344] Department of State Hospitals from counties across the state. Patients receive a full evaluation upon admission to determine  

[11:2:66,353] whether they can be treated through the Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center on a short-term basis or may need  

[11:3:66,363] longer-term state hospital treatment. Patients considered to be short-term can be treated and discharged directly from the  

[11:4:66,373] Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center.  

[12:0:66,390] 4430020 - JAIL-BASED COMPETENCY TREATMENT  

[13:0:66,407] The Jail-Based Competency Treatment Program focuses on defendants deemed incompetent to stand trial and provides  

[13:1:66,417] mental health treatment to defendants in county jails, restoring them to competency, and allowing for participation in court  

[13:2:66,427] proceedings. 

[14:0:66,444] 4430030 - OTHER CONTRACTED SERVICES  

[15:0:66,461] The Other Contracted Services includes additional contracts with local entities to provide mental health services to some of its  

[15:1:66,471] patients outside of state hospital facilities. Programs include IST Diversion and Community-Based Restoration programs. 

[16:0:66,489] 4430040 - The Other Contracted Services focuses on policy development, program management and oversight of Jail Based  

[16:1:66,498] Treatment Programs and Community Based IST Programs.  

[17:0:66,516] 4430050 - The Jail Based Treatment Programs focus on defendants deemed IST on felony charges and provides mental health  

[17:1:66,525] treatment to these individuals in county jails, restoring them to competency, and allowing for participation in court proceedings.  

[18:0:66,543] 4430060 - The Community Based Incompetent to Stand Trial programs are partnerships with various counties to treat felony  

[18:1:66,552] IST in a community mental health treatment setting. This includes Community-Based Restoration, Diversion and Community  

[18:2:66,562] Inpatient Facilities.  

[19:0:66,579] 4440 - EVALUATION AND FORENSIC SERVICES  

[20:0:66,597] Evaluation and Forensic Services is comprised of the   OMD and the Sex Offender Commitment Programs. Penal Code  

[20:1:66,606] Sections 2960-2981 require that a prisoner who meets specific criteria be ordered by the Board of Parole Hearings to be  

[20:2:66,616] treated by State Hospitals as a condition of parole. The Department of State Hospitals performs evaluations to determine if  

[20:3:66,626] individuals may meet the statutory criteria for the   OMD program. These evaluations are used by the Board of Parole Hearings  

[20:4:66,636] in determining whether a prisoner is committed to the Department of State Hospitals as a condition of parole. Welfare and  

[20:5:66,646] Institutions Code Section 6600 et seq. (Chapter 793, Statutes of 1995) was enacted January 1, 1996, establishing a new  

[20:6:66,655] category of civil commitment for persons found, upon release from prison, to be an SVP. The Sex Offender Commitment  

[20:7:66,665] Program administers clinical screenings and performs evaluations to determine if prisoners may meet the statutory criteria for  

[20:8:66,675] an SVP commitment to the Department of State Hospitals upon completion of their prison term. Superior Courts make the  

[20:9:66,685] ultimate determination whether an individual is likely to be an SVP and warrants forensic psychological evaluations by the  

[20:10:66,694] Department of State Hospitals.  

[21:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[5:0:66,201] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,220] 4170 - The Commission, established in 2004, provides oversight and accountability for portions of the Mental Health Services  

[6:1:66,230] Act (MHSA), Adult and Older Adult System of Care Act, Children’s Mental Health Services Act, and Mental Health Student  

[6:2:66,240] Services Act. The Commission’s primary roles include:  

[6:3:66,257] Program Review, Oversight and Accountability  

[7:0:66,274] The Commission provides oversight, review, training, technical assistance, accountability, and evaluation of specified mental  

[7:1:66,284] health projects and programs supported with MHSA funds.   This includes review and approval of county mental health  

[7:2:66,294] Innovation Programs   and Expenditure Plans.   It also includes assessing whether services that are provided pursuant to the  

[7:3:66,303] MHSA are cost-effective and in accordance with recommended best practices.  

[7:4:66,321] Policy Projects 

[8:0:66,338] The Commission may advise the Governor and the Legislature regarding actions the state may take to improve care and  

[8:1:66,348] services for   individuals living   with mental illness. The Commission executes projects designed to inform mental health policy by  

[8:2:66,358] integrating research findings and experiential knowledge. The Commission’s projects include criminal justice mental health, the  

[8:3:66,367] state suicide prevention plan, workplace mental health standards, prevention and early intervention strategies, and school-

[8:4:66,377] based mental health.  

[8:5:66,394] Strategic Partnerships  

[9:0:66,412] The Commission partners with universities, institutes, and public agencies to develop, field-test and implement changes and  

[9:1:66,421] policy solutions. The Commission’s partnerships include the Full Service Partnership Pilot, the Early Psychosis Learning Health  

[9:2:66,431] Care Network, the Youth Innovation Project, the Innovation Incubator project, and the suicide crisis center project.  

[9:3:66,449] Grant Programs  

[10:0:66,466] The Commission manages grant programs that incentivize stronger partnerships, integrated services, braided funding and the  

[10:1:66,476] evaluation required for continuous improvement. The Commission’s grant programs include the Mental Health Wellness Act of  

[10:2:66,485] 2013 crisis prevention, early intervention, and crisis response grants, youth drop-in centers, the early psychosis project, and the

[10:0:66,563] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[10:1:66,582] 4181 - ENERGY PROGRAMS  

[11:0:66,600] The Energy Programs assist low-income households in meeting their immediate and long-term home energy needs through  

[11:1:66,609] financial assistance, energy conservation, weatherization and renewable energy services.  

[12:0:66,627] The Low-Income Home Energy Assistance Program (LIHEAP) provides financial assistance to eligible low-income households  

[12:1:66,636] to offset the costs of heating and/or cooling residential dwellings, assistance for weather-related or energy-related  

[12:2:66,646] emergencies, and weatherization services to improve the energy efficiency of low-income residential dwellings and safeguard  

[12:3:66,656] the health and safety of household occupants. This program may include a leveraging incentive program in which  

[12:4:66,666] supplementary LIHEAP funds can be obtained by LIHEAP grantees if non-federal leveraged home energy resources are used  

[12:5:66,675] along with LIHEAP weatherization related services.  

[13:0:66,693] The Low Income Household Water Assistance Program is designed to provide financial assistance to low-income households  

[13:1:66,703] that pay a high proportion of household income for drinking water and wastewater services, by providing funds to owners or  

[13:2:66,712] operators of public water systems or treatment works to reduce arrearages of, and rates charged to, such households for these  

[14:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 164 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — HHS   162 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:99,32] 4700   Department of Community Services and Development - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] services.  

[4:0:66,88] The Department of Energy Weatherization Assistance Program provides weatherization to improve the energy efficiency of low-

[4:1:66,98] income residential dwellings and safeguard the health and safety of household occupants.  

[5:0:66,115] The Low-Income Weatherization Program (LIWP) provides energy efficiency and renewable energy services in low-income  

[5:1:66,125] single-family and multi-family dwellings to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and lower energy costs. LIWP projects include  

[5:2:66,135] weatherization and solar photovoltaic systems installations.  

[6:0:66,152] The California Arrearage Payment Program is designed to prevent energy utility disconnections for households experiencing  

[6:1:66,162] financial hardship due to the economic impacts of the COVID-19 pandemic by providing financial assistance to customer  

[6:2:66,171] accounts in arrears.  

[6:3:66,189] 4185 - COMMUNITY SERVICES  

[7:0:66,206] The Community Services Block Grant (CSBG) is designed to enable local government and private nonprofit community  

[7:1:66,216] organizations to help low-income families achieve and maintain economic security through a broad range of activities. These  

[7:2:66,226] activities include education, employment services, emergency services, housing, income support and management, and health  

[7:3:66,235] and nutritional services. Additionally, CSBG funds are used by local community organizations to revitalize low-income  

[7:4:66,245] communities.  

[8:0:66,262] The California Earned Income Tax Credit (CalEITC) benefits low-income, working Californians by providing cash-back tax  

[8:1:66,272] credits to boost the income of eligible individuals and families. Since 2017-18,   the Department   has worked with the Franchise  

[8:2:66,282] Tax Board to provide grant opportunities for community-based organizations to increase awareness of CalEITC.

[0:0:66,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — HHS   172 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:170,32] 5160   Department of Rehabilitation - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,84] 4210 - VOCATIONAL REHABILITATION SERVICES  

[5:0:66,101] The Vocational Rehabilitation Services Program delivers vocational rehabilitation services to individuals with disabilities through  

[5:1:66,111] vocational rehabilitation professionals in district and branch offices located throughout the state so that individuals with  

[5:2:66,121] disabilities may prepare for and engage in competitive integrated employment and achieve economic self-sufficiency. In  

[5:3:66,130] addition, the Department has cooperative agreements with state and local agencies (secondary and postsecondary education,  

[5:4:66,140] behavioral/mental health, and welfare) to provide services to consumers. The Department operates under a federal Order of  

[5:5:66,150] Selection process, which gives priority to individuals with the most significant disabilities.  

[6:0:66,167] Individuals with disabilities who are eligible for the Department's vocational rehabilitation services may be provided a full range  

[6:1:66,177] of services, including vocational assessment, assistive technology, vocational and educational training, job placement,  

[6:2:66,187] supported employment and independent living skills training to maximize their ability to live and work independently within their  

[6:3:66,196] communities. The Department provides Work Incentives Planning services to reduce dependency on public benefits. The  

[6:4:66,206] Department provides career counseling and information and referral services to encourage individuals working in non-

[6:5:66,216] competitive, non-integrated settings to work toward and achieve competitive integrated employment.  

[7:0:66,233] The Department additionally provides pre-employment transition student services, known as DOR Student Services, and  

[7:1:66,243] auxiliary aids and services necessary to participate in such services to a wide range of students with disabilities, ages 16 up to  

[7:2:66,253] 22 (depending on their exit from their special education program), including many who may benefit from early career  

[7:3:66,263] development. DOR Student Services include job exploration counseling, work-based learning experiences, postsecondary  

[7:4:66,272] education counseling, workplace readiness training, and instruction in self-advocacy. 

[8:0:66,290] The Department, through its Business Enterprises Program, provides comprehensive training and technical assistance to  

[8:1:66,299] enable individuals who are blind or visually impaired to support themselves in the operation of vending stands, snack bars, and  

[8:2:66,309] cafeterias. Prevocational, including employment readiness, services are provided by the Orientation Center for the Blind to  

[8:3:66,319] consumers with vision loss to prepare them for independent living.  

[9:0:66,336] The Department works with public and private organizations to develop and improve community-based vocational rehabilitation  

[9:1:66,346] services for the Department's consumers. The Department sets standards, certifies Community Rehabilitation Programs, and  

[9:2:66,356] establishes fees for services provided to its consumers.  

[10:0:66,373] The Department, in partnership with the Department of Developmental Services, implements strategic initiatives to increase the  

[10:1:66,383] employment of individuals with disabilities through the Disability Employment Program. The Department initiates a targeted  

[10:2:66,393] marketing campaign and incentivizes employers to hire individuals with disabilities through technical assistance, workplace  

[10:3:66,402] accessibility, and support training.  

[11:0:66,420] 4215 - INDEPENDENT LIVING SERVICES  

[12:0:66,437] The Department funds, administers, and supports 28 non-profit independent living centers in communities located throughout  

[12:1:66,447] California. Each independent living center provides services necessary to assist consumers to live independently   with full  

[12:2:66,457] inclusion   in their communities. Core services consist of information and referral, peer counseling, individual and systems  

[12:3:66,466] change advocacy, independent living skills, housing assistance, personal assistance referral services, transition and diversion  

[12:4:66,476] services to community-based living, and   transition services to postsecondary life for youth.  

[13:0:66,493] The Department administers and supports the Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI) Program. In coordination with consumers and their  

[13:1:66,503] families, six service providers throughout California provide a coordinated post-acute care service model for individuals with  

[13:2:66,513] TBI, including supported living, community reintegration, vocational supportive services, public awareness, and support for  

[13:3:66,523] family, friends, and professionals within the TBI community. The Department also works with the federal government to  

[13:4:66,532] administer a TBI partnership grant with which a state TBI Advisory Board has been established for the purpose of creating a  

[13:5:66,542] TBI state plan, sustainability plan, statewide TBI registry, and needs assessment.  

[14:0:66,559] In addition, the Department expands the capacity of existing TBI sites and stand up new TBI sites in alignment with Home and  

[14:1:66,569] Community-Based Services surrounding transition and diversion through community reintegration, personal care services  

[14:2:66,579] through supported living services, and other supportive services to improve functional capabilities of individuals with TBI.  

[15:0:66,596] The Department administers the federal Older Individuals Who Are Blind program that supports 17 non-profit community-based  

[15:1:66,606] organizations throughout California that provide blindness-related independent living services necessary to assist visually  

[15:2:66,616] impaired consumers age 55 or older to live independently and be productive in their communities. Core services consist of low  

[15:3:66,626] vision evaluations/screenings, assistive technology devices and training, orientation and mobility, communication skills,  

[15:4:66,635] independent living skills training, self-advocacy, adjustment counseling, transportation, and supportive services.  

[16:0:66,653] Through a partnership with the California Public Utilities Commission’s Deaf and Disabled Telecommunications Program, the  

[16:1:66,662] Department’s Voice Options program provides eligible Californians who are unable to speak, or who have difficulty speaking,  

[16:2:66,672] with a free speech-generating device. The goal of this program is to ensure full and equal telephone communications access  

[16:3:66,682] for all Californians with disabilities.  

[17:0:66,699] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION  

[18:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[5:0:66,214] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,232] 4250 - STATE COUNCIL SERVICES  

[6:0:66,252] The State Independent Living Council is responsible for developing a state plan for independent living and for monitoring,  

[6:1:66,262] reviewing and evaluating the implementation of that plan. The Council also interacts with similar statewide councils to enhance  

[6:2:66,272] the effectiveness of the network of centers that provide independent living services in California. The Council is required by the  

[6:3:66,281] Federal Rehabilitation Act of 1973, as amended, in order for the state to receive financial assistance for Independent Living  

[6:4:66,291] Services and the Centers for Independent Living. The Council serves as an educational resource on disability and independent  

[6:5:66,301] living for the Governor, other state agencies, the Legislature, the general public, and a variety of statewide and national  

[6:6:66,311] organizations.

[2:0:144,32] 5175   Department of Child Support Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,84] 4260 - CHILD SUPPORT SERVICES PROGRAM  

[4:0:66,101] The Child Support Services program establishes the system and process for encouraging and, when necessary, enforcing  

[4:1:66,111] parental responsibilities by establishing paternity for children, establishing court orders for financial and medical support, and  

[4:2:66,121] enforcing those orders. The program operates as the single state entity designed to administer the federally mandated Title IV-

[4:3:66,130] D child support program in California. Operation of this program is required for the state to continue to receive the Temporary  

[4:4:66,140] Assistance for Needy Families block grant.  

[4:5:66,157] 4260010 - CHILD SUPPORT ADMINISTRATION:  

[5:0:66,175] The Child Support Administration program provides funding for the salaries and benefits for local and state staff, and operating  

[5:1:66,184] expenses and equipment for the operation of California's child support program, including local child support agencies. The  

[5:2:66,194] federal government provides 66 percent of the funding and the state funds 34 percent of the administration costs.  

[5:3:66,211] 4260019 - CHILD SUPPORT AUTOMATION:  

[6:0:66,229] Pursuant to Federal law, the Department created a single, statewide child support automation system that meets federal  

[6:1:66,239] certification. There are two components of the statewide system: the Child Support Enforcement system and the State  

[6:2:66,248] Disbursement Unit. The enforcement system provides local child support staff tools to manage child support customer accounts  

[6:3:66,258] and locate and intercept assets of non-custodial parents delinquent in their child support payments. The Child Support  

[6:4:66,268] Automation program provides funding for the vendor-operated state disbursement unit, which collects child support payments  

[6:5:66,278] from non-custodial parents and disburses payments to custodial parties. In addition, the Child Support Automation program  

[6:6:66,287] provides funding for electronic data processing maintenance and operation costs at local agencies.
