[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:407,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — HHS   191 

[2:0:166,32] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,84] 4270 - WELFARE PROGRAMS  

[5:0:66,101] The Department's public assistance programs provide financial assistance to California residents who are unable to support  

[5:1:66,111] themselves. These programs are comprised of five components:  

[6:0:65,128] • California Work Opportunity and Responsibility to Kids (CalWORKs)  

[7:0:65,144] • Other Assistance Payments, including Foster Care, Adoption Assistance Program, Refugee Cash Assistance, and Food  

[7:1:76,154] Assistance Programs  

[8:0:65,169] • Supplemental Security Income/State Supplementary Payment Program  

[9:0:65,185] • County Administration and Automation Projects  

[10:0:65,201] • Disaster Relief  

[11:0:66,218] The objectives of these programs are to provide temporary financial assistance to eligible needy and dependent persons to  

[11:1:66,228] enable achievement of self-sufficiency or to provide safe living environments for vulnerable adults and children, and to monitor,  

[11:2:66,238] administer, and improve the quality of all welfare services.  

[12:0:66,255] 4270010 - CalWORKs:  

[13:0:66,272] The CalWORKs program is California's version of the federal Temporary Assistance for Needy Families program. CalWORKs is  

[13:1:66,282] California's largest cash aid program for children and families and is designed to provide temporary assistance to meet basic  

[13:2:66,292] needs, such as shelter, food, and clothing, in times of crisis, while encouraging personal responsibility. CalWORKs includes  

[13:3:66,302] specific welfare-to-work requirements and provides supportive services, such as child care, to enable an individual to meet  

[13:4:66,311] these requirements. Child care services currently are provided through a three-stage system to current and former CalWORKs  

[13:5:66,321] recipients with children through the age of 10 (or up to 12 under certain conditions). Parents have the right to choose child care  

[13:6:66,331] among center-based, family child care homes, or license-exempt providers. CalWORKs families are then able to meet both  

[13:7:66,341] goals of moving from welfare into the work force and engaging children in child care and development services.  

[14:0:66,358] 4270019 - Other Assistance Payments:  

[15:0:66,375] The Foster Care program provides assistance payments to relatives, foster family homes, foster family agencies, short-term  

[15:1:66,385] residential treatment centers or group homes for children who have been removed from the custody of a parent or guardian as  

[15:2:66,395] a result of a judicial order or voluntary placement agreement due to findings of abuse, neglect or exploitation. This program is  

[15:3:66,405] administered by the counties in accordance with regulations, standards, and procedures set by the Department of Social  

[15:4:66,414] Services as authorized by federal and state law.  

[16:0:66,432] The Kinship Guardianship Assistance Program provides support payments to relative guardians of children who were  

[16:1:66,441] previously in the foster care system.  

[17:0:66,459] The Adoption Assistance Program provides financial assistance to families adopting a child with special needs or to facilitate  

[17:1:66,468] the adoption of children who otherwise would remain in long-term foster care. This program is administered by the counties in  

[17:2:66,478] accordance with regulations, standards, and procedures set by the Department of Social Services as authorized by federal and  

[17:3:66,488] state law.  

[18:0:66,505] California also provides cash assistance to eligible refugee/entrant populations via the following programs:  

[19:0:65,523] • The Refugee Cash Assistance provides cash grants to refugees/entrants in their first eight months in the United States  

[19:1:76,532] provided they are not otherwise eligible for categorical welfare programs.  

[20:0:65,548] • The Unaccompanied Refugee Minors program provides culturally and linguistically appropriate child welfare, foster care, and  

[20:1:76,558] independent living services to minors who do not have parents in the United States, or who enter the United States  

[20:2:76,568] unaccompanied by a parent, an immediate adult relative, or an adult having documentable legal evidence of custody of the  

[20:3:76,577] minor.  

[21:0:65,593] • The Trafficking and Crime Victims Assistance Program provides cash aid and social services to noncitizen victims of human  

[21:1:76,603] trafficking, domestic violence and other serious crimes who meet the income and eligibility requirements. Benefits are  

[21:2:76,613] available for a maximum period of eight months for adults without children and up to 48 months for families (under  

[21:3:76,623] CalWORKs).  

[22:0:66,640] The CalFresh Program, federally referred to as the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program, provides improved levels of  

[22:1:66,650] nutrition among eligible low-income households by offering them a benefit amount, posted to a debit card, for the purpose of  

[22:2:66,659] purchasing food. The cost of CalFresh benefits is provided by the United States Department of Agriculture for populations  

[22:3:66,669] eligible to receive federal benefits. Legal immigrants who meet program eligibility criteria but are ineligible for federal benefits  

[22:4:66,679] due to their immigration status are served under the state-funded program known as the California Food Assistance Program.  

[22:5:66,689] The CalFresh Employment and Training Program allows certain non-assistance CalFresh recipients to participate in  

[22:6:66,698] employment and training activities.  

[23:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 194 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — HHS   192 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:166,32] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] The Emergency Food Assistance Program provides commodities to local food banks in all 58 California counties for distribution  

[3:1:66,78] to the working poor, low-income, unemployed, and homeless persons. The food is distributed to eligible recipients for  

[3:2:66,88] household consumption or used to prepare and serve meals in congregate settings. This program is also supplemented with  

[3:3:66,98] food purchased by food banks using private donations, funds provided by the state, taxpayer contributions generated through a  

[3:4:66,108] state income tax check-off, as well as surplus fresh fruits and vegetables donated by farmers and businesses.  

[4:0:66,125] The Commodity Supplemental Food Program is a federally funded program for local non-profit agencies to provide nutritious  

[4:1:66,135] supplemental foods to low-income, elderly people at least 60 years of age. Administrative responsibility for the Commodity  

[4:2:66,144] Supplemental Food Program was transferred from the California Department of Education to the Department of Social Services  

[4:3:66,154] on October 1, 2016.  

[5:0:66,171] 4270020 - Child Care and Development:  

[6:0:66,189] The Child Care and Development program reflects services transitioned to the Department of Social Services from the  

[6:1:66,198] Department of Education, effective July 1, 2021. This includes but is not limited to Stages Two and Three of CalWORKs Child  

[6:2:66,208] Care, migrant day care, and Child and Adult Care Food Programs.  

[7:0:66,226] 4270028 - Supplemental Security Income/State Supplementary Payment Program:  

[8:0:66,235] The federal Supplemental Security Income (SSI) program is a cash assistance program for low-income aged, blind, or disabled  

[8:1:66,245] persons who meet the program's income and resource requirements. California supplements the federal SSI payment with a  

[8:2:66,255] State Supplementary Payment (SSP). The SSI/SSP program is administered by the federal Social Security Administration who  

[8:3:66,265] determines eligibility, computes grants, and disburses the combined monthly payment to recipients.  

[9:0:66,282] 4270037 - County Administration and Automation Projects:  

[10:0:66,299] Federal, state, and county governments share the cost of operating expenses and the salaries and benefits of county staff who  

[10:1:66,309] administer public assistance programs.  

[11:0:66,326] Federal, state, and county funds are used to finance major data automation projects of the Department of Social Services.  

[12:0:66,344] 4270046 - Disaster Relief:  

[13:0:66,361] The objective of the Disaster Relief Program is to provide monetary assistance to individuals and households who have  

[13:1:66,371] suffered eligible losses from a Presidentially-declared disaster that are not covered by other federal, state, or private assistance  

[13:2:66,380] programs, and to oversee mass care and shelter, social services recovery, emergency repatriation, and administration of select  

[13:3:66,390] recovery grants.  

[14:0:66,407] 4275 - SOCIAL SERVICES AND LICENSING  

[15:0:66,425] The Department of Social Services oversees and monitors the administration of social services programs, which include child  

[15:1:66,434] welfare, adoptions, licensing and special programs. The department is responsible for development of policy, regulations, and  

[15:2:66,444] procedures that govern the delivery of services to children, families and other recipients, and the monitoring and evaluation of  

[15:3:66,454] the service delivery system.  

[16:0:66,471] 4275010 - In-Home Supportive Services:  

[17:0:66,489] The In-Home Supportive Services (IHSS) program provides in-home services that enable eligible individuals to remain safely in  

[17:1:66,498] their own homes as an alternative to out-of-home care. Eligible persons are low-income aged, blind, or disabled individuals who  

[17:2:66,508] either qualify for federally funded Medi-Cal or meet the program's income and resource requirements. There are four programs  

[17:3:66,518] that provide in-home care: the Personal Care Services Program, IHSS Plus Option Program, Community First Choice Option,  

[17:4:66,528] and IHSS-Residual Program.  

[18:0:66,545] 4275019 - Children and Adult Services and Licensing:  

[19:0:66,562] The Children's Services component consists of three major areas: Child Welfare Services, Adoptions, and Child Abuse  

[19:1:66,572] Prevention.  

[20:0:66,589] Child Welfare Services provides emergency response, family maintenance, family reunification, and permanent placement and  

[20:1:66,599] prevention services to protect abused, neglected or exploited children. The services are provided through an integrated  

[20:2:66,609] services delivery system that provides intensive services to families to promote child safety, permanency and well-being with  

[20:3:66,619] the goal of allowing families to stay together in their own homes, or arrangement for the child's placement in the safest and  

[20:4:66,628] least restrictive home-like setting. Services also include assistance to youth who are emancipating or have emancipated from  

[20:5:66,638] foster care. The program also provides training and technical assistance to county administrators and staff.  

[21:0:66,655] In Child Welfare Services, the Department of Social Services is responsible   for implementing continuum of care  

[21:1:66,665] reforms   codified in Chapter 773, Statutes of 2015. The reforms emphasize home-based family care, improve access to  

[21:2:66,675] services without having to change out-of-home placements to get those services, and increase the role of children, youth, and  

[21:3:66,685] families in assessment and case planning.  

[22:0:66,702] The Adoptions Program provides support services to children and adoptive families through a collaboration of public and  

[22:1:66,712] private adoption agencies in the state. Agency adoptions provide adoption services through public and private agencies for  

[23:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,68] children who have been abused, neglected or exploited and are under the jurisdiction of the county or tribal court. Services  

[3:1:66,78] include adoptive placement screening; home studies; reimbursement of non-recurring adoption expenses for adoptive parents;  

[3:2:66,88] training, recruitment and retention of foster parents; and technical assistance and support for inter-country adoptions. For  

[3:3:66,98] independent adoptions, the public agency investigates a proposed adoption and provides a report to the court when the  

[3:4:66,108] biological parents place their children directly with adoptive parents of their choice.  

[3:5:66,125] The Child Abuse Prevention Program provides funding, training, and technical assistance for the development and  

[3:6:66,135] sustainability of child abuse prevention and early intervention programs, education and outreach materials, activities, and  

[3:7:66,144] services for at risk families and their children.  

[4:0:66,162] The Adult Protective Services program provides funding for counties to address reports of abuse, neglect, or financial  

[4:1:66,171] exploitation of elder or dependent adults and provide intervention, as necessary.  

[5:0:66,189] The Community Care Licensing Program is a regulatory enforcement program with the responsibility of protecting the health  

[5:1:66,198] and safety of children and adults residing in or spending a portion of their time in out-of-home care. The program includes  

[5:2:66,208] facility licensure, prevention, compliance, and enforcement components.  

[5:3:66,226] 4275028 - Special Programs:  

[6:0:66,243] These programs include but are not limited to programs such as Foster Care Burial, Assistance Dog Special Allowance,  

[6:1:66,253] Access Assistance to the Deaf, Housing Program, Refugee Programs, Immigration and Naturalization Assistance Services,  

[6:2:66,262] and Legal Services for Unaccompanied and Undocumented Minors.  

[6:3:66,280] 4285 - DISABILITY EVALUATION AND OTHER SERVICES  

[7:0:66,297] The objective of this program is to determine an applicant's medical and/or vocational eligibility for disability benefits and  

[7:1:66,307] provide administrative services to other agencies.  

[7:2:66,324] 4285010 - Disability Evaluation:  

[8:0:66,341] The Disability Evaluation Program determines the medical, vocational, and/or functional eligibility of California residents  

[8:1:66,351] applying for benefits under Title II (Disability Insurance), Title XVI (Supplemental Security Income), and Title XIX (Medicaid) of  

[8:2:66,361] the Social Security Act. Eligibility is determined by the severity of the individual's physical and/or mental impairment(s) and  

[8:3:66,371] overall ability to engage in substantial gainful employment.  

[8:4:66,388] 4285019 - Services to Other Agencies:  

[9:0:66,405] In addition to providing support services for its programs, the Department of Social Services provides general administrative  

[9:1:66,415] services, such as personnel and accounting to the State Council on Developmental Disabilities and the Health and Human  

[9:2:66,425] Services Agency. The Department provides services to the Medi-Cal Program in the form of state hearings and public  

[9:3:66,434] information services.

[2:0:165,32] 5195   State-Local Realignment, 1991 - Continued 

[3:0:66,65] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,84] 4350 - STATE-LOCAL REALIGNMENT  

[5:0:66,103] The objectives of Realignment are to assign program responsibility to the most appropriate level of government and achieve  

[5:1:66,113] improved service levels with broad discretion given to the responsible entity. Realignment provides for greater funding stability  

[5:2:66,123] for selected programs, increased local flexibility in administering these programs, and productive fiscal incentives to encourage  

[5:3:66,133] cost-effective approaches to providing services.  

[6:0:66,152] Total Realignment revenues are comprised of a half cent sales tax and a dedicated portion of vehicle license fee revenues.  

[6:1:66,162] Revenues are deposited into the Local Revenue Fund, which includes several accounts. Funds deposited in these accounts  

[6:2:66,172] are continuously appropriated for allocation to local governments according to formula and are used to fund programs specified  

[6:3:66,181] in realignment legislation. The legislation also includes local maintenance of effort and matching requirements in order to  

[6:4:66,191] ensure that counties do not use the realigned funds to supplant local expenditure levels prior to realignment. This provision  

[6:5:66,201] ensures compliance with other state and federal statutes which, in turn, provide hundreds of millions of dollars annually for  

[6:6:66,211] county health and social services programs.  

[7:0:66,250] DETAIL OF APPROPRIATIONS AND ADJUSTMENTS

[11:0:202,495] 5196   2011 State-Local Realignment  

[12:0:66,516] Building upon the 1991-92 Realignment, 2011 Realignment moves program and fiscal responsibility to counties, providing a  

[12:1:66,525] dedicated source of funding while eliminating duplication of effort, generating savings, and increasing flexibility.  

[12:2:66,543] Realigned programs include local public safety programs, mental health, substance abuse, foster care, child welfare services,  

[12:3:66,552] and adult protective services. Many of these programs are already administered at the local level by counties. Therefore, it is  

[12:4:66,562] appropriate for the programmatic and fiscal responsibility to reside with the counties with the state maintaining an oversight and  

[12:5:66,572] technical assistance role where needed. These changes are made with the goal of providing services more efficiently and at  

[12:6:66,582] less cost.  

[12:7:66,599] The funding sources for realignment are:  

[12:8:65,616] • The dedication of 1.0625 cents of a state special fund sales tax.  

[12:9:65,632] • The dedication of a portion of vehicle license fee revenues.  

[12:10:66,649] Counties receive 2011 Realignment funding from the following accounts and their related growth accounts:  

[12:11:65,667] • Protective Services Subaccount (Foster Care, Child Welfare Services, and Adult Protective Services)  

[12:12:65,682] • Behavioral Health Subaccount (Early and Periodic Screening, Diagnosis, and Treatment; Mental Health Managed Care;  

[12:13:76,692] Substance Abuse Treatment; and Women and Children's Residential Treatment)  

[12:14:65,708] • Mental Health Account (Community Mental Health Programs)  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.
